</td>
<td>571
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png/280px-Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png" width="280" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png/420px-Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png/560px-Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png 2x" data-file-width="912" data-file-height="456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_state-school_students_at_Oxford_and_Cambridge.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Percentage of state-school students at Oxford and Cambridge<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In common with most British universities, prospective students apply through the <a href="/wiki/UCAS" title="UCAS">UCAS</a> application system, but prospective applicants for the University of Oxford, along with those for medicine, dentistry, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> applicants, must observe an earlier deadline of 15 October.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To allow a more personalised judgement of students, who might otherwise apply for both, undergraduate applicants are not permitted to apply to both Oxford and Cambridge in the same year. The only exceptions are applicants for <a href="/wiki/Organ_scholar" title="Organ scholar">organ scholarships</a><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> and those applying to read for a second undergraduate degree.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most applicants choose to apply to one of the individual colleges, which work with each other to ensure that the best students gain a place somewhere at the university regardless of their college preferences.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Shortlisting is based on achieved and predicted exam results, school references, and, in some subjects, written admission tests or candidate-submitted written work. Approximately 60% of applicants are shortlisted, although this varies by subject. If a large number of shortlisted applicants for a subject choose one college, then students who named that college may be reallocated randomly to under-subscribed colleges for the subject. The colleges then invite shortlisted candidates for interview, where they are provided with food and accommodation for around three days in December. Most applicants will be individually interviewed by academics at more than one college. Students from outside Europe can be interviewed remotely, for example, over the Internet.
</p><p>Offers are sent out in early January, with each offer usually being from a specific college. One in four successful candidates receives an offer from a college that they did not apply to. Some courses may make "open offers" to some candidates, who are not assigned to a particular college until <a href="/wiki/A_Level" class="mw-redirect" title="A Level">A Level</a> results day in August.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university has come under criticism for the number of students it accepts from <a href="/wiki/Private_school" title="Private school">private schools</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> for instance, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Spence_Affair" title="Laura Spence Affair">Laura Spence</a>'s rejection from the university in 2000 led to widespread debate.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the University of Oxford gave 59% of offers to UK students to students from state schools, while about 93% of all UK pupils and 86% of post-16 UK pupils are educated in state schools.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_state_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_state-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OU_Facts_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OU_Facts-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Post16Ind_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Post16Ind-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> However, 64% of UK applicants were from state schools and the university notes that state school students apply disproportionately to oversubscribed subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Oxford University spends over £6 million per year on outreach programs to encourage applicants from underrepresented demographics.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_state_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_state-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018 the university's annual admissions report revealed that approximately one third of Oxford's colleges had accepted three or fewer black applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Lammy" title="David Lammy">David Lammy</a> said, “This is social apartheid and it is utterly unrepresentative of life in modern Britain.”<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaching_and_degrees">Teaching and degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Teaching and degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_the_University_of_Oxford" title="Degrees of the University of Oxford">Degrees of the University of Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_professorships_at_the_University_of_Oxford" title="List of professorships at the University of Oxford">List of professorships at the University of Oxford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education_at_University_of_Oxford" title="Undergraduate education at University of Oxford">Undergraduate education at University of Oxford</a></div>
<p>Undergraduate teaching is centred on the tutorial, where 1–4 students spend an hour with an academic discussing their week's work, usually an essay (humanities, most social sciences, some mathematical, physical, and life sciences) or problem sheet (most mathematical, physical, and life sciences, and some social sciences). The university itself is responsible for conducting examinations and conferring degrees. Undergraduate teaching takes place during three eight-week academic terms: <a href="/wiki/Michaelmas_term" title="Michaelmas term">Michaelmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hilary_term" title="Hilary term">Hilary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinity_term" title="Trinity term">Trinity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> (These are officially known as 'Full Term': 'Term' is a lengthier period with little practical significance.) Internally, the weeks in a term begin on Sundays, and are referred to numerically, with the initial week known as "first week", the last as "eighth week" and with the numbering extended to refer to weeks before and after term (for example "-1st week" and "0th week" precede term). Undergraduates must be in residence from Thursday of 0th week. These teaching terms are shorter than those of most other British universities,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and their total duration amounts to less than half the year. However, undergraduates are also expected to do some academic work during the three holidays (known as the Christmas, Easter, and Long Vacations).
</p><p>Research degrees at the master's and doctoral level are conferred in all subjects studied at graduate level at the university. 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholarships_and_financial_support">Scholarships and financial support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Scholarships and financial support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg/220px-Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg/330px-Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg/440px-Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_House_Oxford_20040909.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rhodes_House" title="Rhodes House">Rhodes House</a> – home to the awarding body for the <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarships</a>, often considered to be the world's most prestigious scholarship</div></div></div>
<p>There are many opportunities for students at Oxford to receive financial help during their studies. The Oxford Opportunity Bursaries, introduced in 2006, are university-wide means-based bursaries available to any British undergraduate, with a total possible grant of £10,235 over a 3-year degree. In addition, individual colleges also offer bursaries and funds to help their students. For graduate study, there are many scholarships attached to the university, available to students from all sorts of backgrounds, from <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarships</a> to the relatively new Weidenfeld Scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Oxford also offers the <a href="/wiki/Clarendon_Fund" title="Clarendon Fund">Clarendon Scholarship</a> which is open to graduate applicants of all nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The Clarendon Scholarship is principally funded by <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a> in association with colleges and other partnership awards.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Oxford University announced that it is to run its first free online economics course as part of a “<a href="/wiki/Massive_open_online_course" title="Massive open online course">massive open online course</a>" (Mooc) scheme, in partnership with a US online university network.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The course available is called ‘From Poverty to Prosperity: Understanding Economic Development’.
</p><p>Students successful in early examinations are rewarded by their colleges with scholarships and <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_(scholarship)" title="Exhibition (scholarship)">exhibitions</a>, normally the result of a long-standing endowment, although since the introduction of tuition fees the amounts of money available are purely nominal. Scholars, and exhibitioners in some colleges, are entitled to wear a more voluminous undergraduate gown; "commoners" (originally those who had to pay for their "commons", or food and lodging) are restricted to a short, sleeveless garment. The term "scholar" in relation to Oxford therefore has a specific meaning as well as the more general meaning of someone of outstanding academic ability. In previous times, there were "noblemen commoners" and "gentlemen commoners", but these ranks were abolished in the 19th century. "Closed" scholarships, available only to candidates who fitted specific conditions such as coming from specific schools, were abolished in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-Crook_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crook-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Libraries_of_the_University_of_Oxford" title="Category:Libraries of the University of Oxford">Category:Libraries of the University of Oxford</a></div>
<p>The university maintains the largest university library system in the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-uls_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uls-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and, with over 11&#160;million volumes housed on 120 miles (190&#160;km) of shelving, the Bodleian group is the second-largest library in the UK, after the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>. The Bodleian is a <a href="/wiki/Legal_deposit" title="Legal deposit">legal deposit</a> library, which means that it is entitled to request a free copy of every book published in the UK. As such, its collection is growing at a rate of over three miles (five kilometres) of shelving every year.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The buildings referred to as the university's main research library, <a href="/wiki/Bodleian_Library" title="Bodleian Library">The Bodleian</a>, consist of the original Bodleian Library in the Old Schools Quadrangle, founded by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bodley" title="Thomas Bodley">Sir Thomas Bodley</a> in 1598 and opened in 1602,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Radcliffe_Camera" title="Radcliffe Camera">Radcliffe Camera</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Clarendon_Building" title="Clarendon Building">Clarendon Building</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Weston_Library" title="Weston Library">Weston Library</a>. A tunnel underneath <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street,_Oxford" title="Broad Street, Oxford">Broad Street</a> connects these buildings, with the Gladstone Link, which opened to readers in 2011, connecting the Old Bodleian and Radcliffe Camera.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Clarendon_Building_3_(5649801503).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Old_Clarendon_Building_3_%285649801503%29.jpg/220px-Old_Clarendon_Building_3_%285649801503%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Old_Clarendon_Building_3_%285649801503%29.jpg/330px-Old_Clarendon_Building_3_%285649801503%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Old_Clarendon_Building_3_%285649801503%29.jpg/440px-Old_Clarendon_Building_3_%285649801503%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Clarendon_Building_3_(5649801503).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Clarendon_Building" title="Clarendon Building">Clarendon Building</a> is home to many senior Bodleian Library staff and previously housed the university's own central administration</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bodleian_Libraries" title="Bodleian Libraries">Bodleian Libraries</a> group was formed in 2000, bringing the Bodleian Library and some of the subject libraries together.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> It now comprises 28<sup id="cite_ref-Bodleian_Libraries_list_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodleian_Libraries_list-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> libraries, a number of which have been created by bringing previously separate collections together, including the <a href="/wiki/Sackler_Library" title="Sackler Library">Sackler Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bodleian_Social_Science_Library,_Oxford" class="mw-redirect" title="Bodleian Social Science Library, Oxford">Social Science Library</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radcliffe_Science_Library" title="Radcliffe Science Library">Radcliffe Science Library</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Another major product of this collaboration has been a joint integrated library system, <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Libraries_Information_System" title="Oxford Libraries Information System">OLIS</a> (<b>O</b>xford <b>L</b>ibraries <b>I</b>nformation <b>S</b>ystem),<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and its public interface, <b>SOLO</b> (<b>S</b>earch <b>O</b>xford <b>L</b>ibraries <b>O</b>nline), which provides an electronic catalogue covering all member libraries, as well as the libraries of individual colleges and other faculty libraries, which are not members of the group but do share cataloguing information.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A new book depository opened in <a href="/wiki/South_Marston" title="South Marston">South Marston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swindon" title="Swindon">Swindon</a> in October 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and recent building projects include the remodelling of the New Bodleian building, which was renamed the Weston Library when it reopened in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Weston_Library_Open_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weston_Library_Open-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The renovation is designed to better showcase the library's various treasures (which include a Shakespeare <a href="/wiki/First_Folio" title="First Folio">First Folio</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Gutenberg_Bible" title="Gutenberg Bible">Gutenberg Bible</a>) as well as temporary exhibitions.
</p><p>The Bodleian engaged in a mass-digitisation project with <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Museums_of_the_University_of_Oxford" title="Category:Museums of the University of Oxford">Category:Museums of the University of Oxford</a></div>
<p>Oxford maintains a number of museums and galleries, open for free to the public. The <a href="/wiki/Ashmolean_Museum" title="Ashmolean Museum">Ashmolean Museum</a>, founded in 1683, is the oldest museum in the UK, and the oldest university museum in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> It holds significant collections of art and archaeology, including works by <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._M._W._Turner" title="J. M. W. Turner">Turner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Picasso</a>, as well as treasures such as the <a href="/wiki/Scorpion_Macehead" title="Scorpion Macehead">Scorpion Macehead</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Parian_Chronicle" title="Parian Chronicle">Parian Marble</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Jewel" title="Alfred Jewel">Alfred Jewel</a>. It also contains "<a href="/wiki/Messiah_Stradivarius" title="Messiah Stradivarius">The Messiah</a>", a pristine Stradivarius violin, regarded by some as one of the finest examples in existence.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Oxford University Museum of Natural History">University Museum of Natural History</a> holds the university's zoological, entomological and geological specimens. It is housed in a large neo-Gothic building on <a href="/wiki/Parks_Road" title="Parks Road">Parks Road</a>, in the university's <a href="/wiki/Science_Area,_Oxford" title="Science Area, Oxford">Science Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Among its collection are the skeletons of a <i><a href="/wiki/Tyrannosaurus" title="Tyrannosaurus">Tyrannosaurus rex</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Triceratops" title="Triceratops">Triceratops</a></i>, and the most complete remains of a <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a> found anywhere in the world. It also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Simonyi" title="Charles Simonyi">Simonyi</a> <a href="/wiki/Simonyi_Professorship_for_the_Public_Understanding_of_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Simonyi Professorship for the Public Understanding of Science">Professorship of the Public Understanding of Science</a>, currently held by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_du_Sautoy" title="Marcus du Sautoy">Marcus du Sautoy</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg/170px-Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg/255px-Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg/340px-Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pitt-rivers-m2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of the <a href="/wiki/Pitt_Rivers_Museum" title="Pitt Rivers Museum">Pitt Rivers Museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>Adjoining the Museum of Natural History is the <a href="/wiki/Pitt_Rivers_Museum" title="Pitt Rivers Museum">Pitt Rivers Museum</a>, founded in 1884, which displays the university's archaeological and anthropological collections, currently holding over 500,000 items. It recently built a new research annexe; its staff have been involved with the teaching of anthropology at Oxford since its foundation, when as part of his donation General <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Pitt_Rivers" title="Augustus Pitt Rivers">Augustus Pitt Rivers</a> stipulated that the university establish a lectureship in anthropology.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_History_of_Science,_Oxford" title="Museum of the History of Science, Oxford">Museum of the History of Science</a> is housed on Broad St in the world's oldest-surviving purpose-built museum building.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> It contains 15,000 artefacts, from antiquity to the 20th century, representing almost all aspects of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">history of science</a>. In the Faculty of Music on <a href="/wiki/St_Aldate%27s,_Oxford" title="St Aldate&#39;s, Oxford">St Aldate's</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Bate_Collection" class="mw-redirect" title="Bate Collection">Bate Collection</a> of Musical Instruments, a collection mostly of instruments from Western classical music, from the medieval period onwards. <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church_Picture_Gallery" title="Christ Church Picture Gallery">Christ Church Picture Gallery</a> holds a collection of over 200 <a href="/wiki/Old_master" class="mw-redirect" title="Old master">old master</a> paintings.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing">Publishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Publishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a></div>
<p>The Oxford University Press is the world's second oldest and currently the largest <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press">university press</a> by the number of publications.<sup id="cite_ref-publishing_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publishing-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> More than 6,000 new books are published annually,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> including many reference, professional, and academic works (such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Concise_Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Concise Oxford English Dictionary">Concise Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_World%27s_Classics" title="Oxford World&#39;s Classics">Oxford World's Classics</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_Dictionary_of_National_Biography" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford Dictionary of National Biography">Oxford Dictionary of National Biography</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Concise_Dictionary_of_National_Biography" class="mw-redirect" title="Concise Dictionary of National Biography">Concise Dictionary of National Biography</a></i>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:23em; text-align:left; font-size:82%;">
<caption style="font-size:125%; font-weight:bold;"><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">Rankings</a></caption>
<tbody><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td colspan="3"><div style="text-align: center;"> <b> Global rankings </b> </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2018_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2018-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><br />
</th><td> 7</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-QS_World_University_Rankings_2019_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS_World_University_Rankings_2019-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><br />
</th><td> 5</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">THE</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-THE_World_University_Rankings_2019_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_World_University_Rankings_2019-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><br />
</th><td> 1</td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td colspan="3"><div style="text-align: center;"> <b><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">National rankings</a></b> </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Complete_University_Guide" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Complete</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_2019_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table_2019-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><br /></th>
<td> 2</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Guardian" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">The Guardian</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2019_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2019-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><br /></th>
<td> 2</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Sunday_Times" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Times / Sunday Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2019_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2019-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><br /></th>
<td> 2</td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td colspan="3"><div style="text-align: center;"> <b> British Government assessment </b> </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Teaching_Excellence_Framework" title="Teaching Excellence Framework">Teaching Excellence Framework</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-TEF_2018_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TEF_2018-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</th><td> <i>Gold</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Oxford is regularly ranked within the top 10 universities in the world and is currently ranked first in the world in the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>'s World University Rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> It held the number one position in the <i>Times Good University Guide</i> for eleven consecutive years,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Medical_School" title="Oxford University Medical School">medical school</a> has also maintained first place in the "Clinical, Pre-Clinical &amp; Health" table of the <i>THE World University Rankings</i> for the past seven consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> <i>THE</i> has also recognised Oxford as one of the world's "six super brands" on its <i>World Reputation Rankings</i>, along with <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">Berkeley</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The university is fifth worldwide on the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report_Best_Global_University_Ranking" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report Best Global University Ranking">US News</a></i> ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Sa%C3%AFd_Business_School" title="Saïd Business School">Saïd Business School</a> came 23rd in the world in <i>Financial Times</i> <i>Global MBA Ranking</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oxford is ranked 5th best university worldwide and 1st in Britain for forming <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a>s according to the <a href="/wiki/Mines_ParisTech_:_Professional_Ranking_World_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Mines ParisTech&#160;: Professional Ranking World Universities"><i>Professional Ranking World Universities</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> It is ranked first in the UK for the quality of its graduates as chosen by the recruiters of the UK's major companies.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Complete_University_Guide" class="mw-redirect" title="Complete University Guide">Complete University Guide</a>, all 38 subjects offered by Oxford rank within the top 10 nationally meaning Oxford was one of only two multi-faculty universities (along with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>) in the UK to have 100% of their subjects in the top 10.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Computer Science, Medicine, Philosophy, Politics and Psychology were ranked first in the UK by the guide.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the QS World University Rankings by Subject, the University of Oxford also ranks as number one in the world for four Humanities disciplines: English Language and Literature, <a href="/wiki/Modern_Languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Languages">Modern Languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">Geography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">History</a>. It also ranks 2nd globally for Anthropology, Archaeology, Law, Medicine, Politics &amp; International Studies, and Psychology.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Academic_dress_of_the_University_of_Oxford" title="Academic dress of the University of Oxford">Academic dress of the University of Oxford</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG/170px-Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG/255px-Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG/340px-Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toby_Virno_sub_fusc.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An undergraduate student at the University of Oxford in <a href="/wiki/Subfusc" class="mw-redirect" title="Subfusc">subfusc</a> for matriculation</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Academic_dress" title="Academic dress">Academic dress</a> is required for examinations, matriculation, disciplinary hearings, and when visiting university officers. A referendum held amongst the Oxford student body in 2015 showed 76% against making it voluntary in examinations – 8,671 students voted, with the 40.2% turnout the highest ever for a UK student union referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> This was widely interpreted by students as being a vote on not so much making <a href="/wiki/Subfusc" class="mw-redirect" title="Subfusc">subfusc</a> voluntary, but rather, in effect, abolishing it by default, in that if a minority of people came to exams without subfusc, the rest would soon follow.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In July 2012 the regulations regarding academic dress were modified to be more inclusive to <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> people.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other traditions and customs vary by college. For example, some colleges have <a href="/wiki/Formal_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Formal hall">formal hall</a> six times a week, but in others this only happens occasionally. At most colleges these formal meals require gowns to be worn, and a Latin grace is said.
</p><p><i>Balls</i> are major events held by colleges; the largest, held triennially in 9th week of Trinity Term, are called <a href="/wiki/Commemoration_ball" title="Commemoration ball">Commemoration balls</a>; the dress code is usually <a href="/wiki/White_tie" title="White tie">white tie</a>. Many other colleges hold smaller events during the year that they call summer balls or parties. These are usually held on an annual or irregular basis, and are usually <a href="/wiki/Black_tie" title="Black tie">black tie</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Punt_(boat)" title="Punt (boat)">Punting</a> is a common summer leisure activity.
</p><p>There are several more or less quirky traditions peculiar to individual colleges, for example the <a href="/wiki/All_Souls_College,_Oxford#Customs" title="All Souls College, Oxford">All Souls mallard song</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clubs_and_societies">Clubs and societies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Clubs and societies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Clubs_and_societies_of_the_University_of_Oxford" title="Category:Clubs and societies of the University of Oxford">Category:Clubs and societies of the University of Oxford</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eights_2005.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Eights_2005.JPG/170px-Eights_2005.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Eights_2005.JPG/255px-Eights_2005.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Eights_2005.JPG/340px-Eights_2005.JPG 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eights_2005.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rowing at Summer Eights, an annual intercollegiate <a href="/wiki/Bumps_race" title="Bumps race">bumps race</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sport is played between college teams, in tournaments known as <a href="/wiki/Cuppers" title="Cuppers">cuppers</a> (the term is also used for some non-sporting competitions). In addition to these there are higher standard <a href="/wiki/Category:Oxford_student_sports_clubs" title="Category:Oxford student sports clubs">university wide groups</a>. Significant focus is given to annual <a href="/wiki/Varsity_match" title="Varsity match">varsity</a> matches played against Cambridge, the most famous of which is <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">The Boat Race</a>, watched by a TV audience of between five and ten million viewers. This outside interest reflects the importance of rowing to many of those within the university. Much attention is given to the termly intercollegiate rowing regattas: Christ Church Regatta, <a href="/wiki/Torpids" title="Torpids">Torpids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Summer_Eights" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Eights">Summer Eights</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Blue_(university_sport)" title="Blue (university sport)">blue</a> is an award given to those who compete at the university team level in certain sports. As well as traditional sports, there are teams for activities such as <a href="/wiki/Octopush" class="mw-redirect" title="Octopush">Octopush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muggle_Quidditch" class="mw-redirect" title="Muggle Quidditch">quidditch</a>.
</p><p>There are two weekly student newspapers: the independent <i><a href="/wiki/Cherwell_(newspaper)" title="Cherwell (newspaper)">Cherwell</a></i> and OUSU's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oxford_Student" title="The Oxford Student">The Oxford Student</a></i>. Other publications include the <a href="/wiki/Isis_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Isis magazine"><i>Isis</i> magazine</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Owl_Journal" title="The Owl Journal">The Owl Journal</a></i>, the satirical <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oxymoron" title="The Oxymoron">Oxymoron</a></i>, and the graduate <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oxonian_Review_of_Books" class="mw-redirect" title="The Oxonian Review of Books">Oxonian Review</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">student radio</a> station is <a href="/wiki/Oxide_Radio" title="Oxide Radio">Oxide Radio</a>. Most colleges have chapel choirs. Music, drama, and other arts societies exist both at collegiate level and as university-wide groups. Unlike most other collegiate societies, musical ensembles actively encourage players from other colleges.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg/220px-UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg/330px-UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg/440px-UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1899" data-file-height="1241" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UnionBuildingsDebateChamber.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Union" title="Oxford Union">Oxford Union</a>'s debating chamber</div></div></div>
<p>Most academic areas have student societies of some form which are open to students studying all courses, for example the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Scientific_Society" title="Oxford University Scientific Society">Scientific Society</a>. There are groups for almost all faiths, political parties, countries and cultures.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Union" title="Oxford Union">Oxford Union</a> (not to be confused with the Oxford University Student Union) hosts weekly debates and high-profile speakers. There have historically been elite invite-only societies such as the <a href="/wiki/Bullingdon_Club" title="Bullingdon Club">Bullingdon Club</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OUSU_and_common_rooms">OUSU and common rooms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: OUSU and common rooms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Student_Union" title="Oxford University Student Union">Oxford University Student Union</a>, better known by its acronym OUSU, exists to represent students in the university's decision-making, to act as the voice for students in the national higher education policy debate, and to provide direct services to the student body. Reflecting the collegiate nature of the University of Oxford itself, OUSU is both an association of Oxford's more than 21,000 individual students and a federation of the affiliated college common rooms, and other affiliated organisations that represent subsets of the undergraduate and graduate students. The OUSU Executive Committee includes six full-time salaried sabbatical officers, who generally serve in the year following completion of their Final Examinations.
</p><p>The importance of collegiate life is such that for many students their college JCR (Junior Common Room, for undergraduates) or MCR (Middle Common Room, for graduates) is seen as more important than OUSU. JCRs and MCRs each have a committee, with a president and other elected students representing their peers to college authorities. Additionally, they organise events and often have significant budgets to spend as they wish (money coming from their colleges and sometimes other sources such as student-run bars). (It is worth noting that JCR and MCR are terms that are used to refer to rooms for use by members, as well as the student bodies.) Not all colleges use this JCR/MCR structure, for example Wadham College's entire student population is represented by a combined Students' Union and purely graduate colleges have different arrangements.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Oxford_people" title="List of University of Oxford people">List of University of Oxford people</a></div>
<p>Throughout its history, a sizeable number of Oxford alumni, known as Oxonians, have become notable in many varied fields, both academic and otherwise, ranging from <a href="/wiki/T._E._Lawrence" title="T. E. Lawrence">T. E. Lawrence</a>, British Army officer known better as <i>Lawrence of Arabia</i><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> to the explorer, courtier, and man of letters, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Sir Walter Raleigh</a>, (who attended <a href="/wiki/Oriel_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriel College">Oriel College</a> but left without taking a degree);<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> and the Australian media mogul, <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Murdoch" title="Rupert Murdoch">Rupert Murdoch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">58 Nobel prize-winners</a> have studied or taught at Oxford, with prizes won in all six categories.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
More information on famous senior and junior members of the university can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Colleges_of_the_University_of_Oxford" title="Colleges of the University of Oxford">individual college</a> articles. An individual may be associated with two or more colleges, as an undergraduate, postgraduate and/or member of staff.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Hugh%27s_College,_Oxford" title="St Hugh&#39;s College, Oxford"> St Hugh's College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>27 British <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">prime ministers</a> have attended Oxford, including <a href="/wiki/William_Gladstone" class="mw-redirect" title="William Gladstone">William Gladstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Heath" title="Edward Heath">Edward Heath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>. Of all the post-war prime ministers, only <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> was educated at a university other than Oxford, while <a href="/wiki/James_Callaghan" title="James Callaghan">James Callaghan</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> never attended a university.<sup id="cite_ref-ebp_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ebp-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over 100 Oxford alumni were elected to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-ebp_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ebp-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> This includes former <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" title="Leader of the Opposition (United Kingdom)">Leader of the Opposition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Miliband" title="Ed Miliband">Ed Miliband</a>, and numerous members of the cabinet and <a href="/wiki/Shadow_cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Shadow cabinet">shadow cabinet</a>. Additionally, over 140 Oxonians sit in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Lords of the United Kingdom">House of Lords</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:380px;max-width:380px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">International leaders who attended Oxford University</div><div class="tsingle" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-18.jpg/230px-Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-18.jpg College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:134px;max-width:134px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" <p>At least 30 other international leaders have been educated at Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This number includes <a href="/wiki/Harald_V_of_Norway" title="Harald V of Norway">Harald V of Norway</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_II_of_Jordan" title="Abdullah II of Jordan">Abdullah II of Jordan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_II_of_the_Netherlands" title="William II of the Netherlands">William II of the Netherlands</a>, five <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Ministers of Australia</a> (<a href="/wiki/John_Gorton" title="John Gorton">John Gorton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Fraser" title="Malcolm Fraser">Malcolm Fraser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hawke" title="Bob Hawke">Bob Hawke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Abbott" title="Tony Abbott">Tony Abbott</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Turnbull" title="Malcolm Turnbull">Malcolm Turnbull</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Six <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan" title="Prime Minister of Pakistan">Prime Ministers of Pakistan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Liaquat_Ali_Khan" title="Liaquat Ali Khan">Liaquat Ali Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huseyn_Shaheed_Suhrawardy" title="Huseyn Shaheed Suhrawardy">Huseyn Shaheed Suhrawardy</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Feroz_Khan_Noon" title="Feroz Khan Noon">Feroz Khan Noon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zulfiqar_Ali_Bhutto" class="mw-redirect" title="Zulfiqar Ali Bhutto">Zulfiqar Ali Bhutto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto" title="Benazir Bhutto">Benazir Bhutto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imran_Khan" title="Imran Khan">Imran Khan</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> two <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Ministers of Canada</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lester_B._Pearson" title="Lester B. Pearson">Lester B. Pearson</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Turner" title="John Turner">John Turner</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> two <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Prime Ministers of India</a> (<a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a>, though the latter did not finish her degree),<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Bandaranaike" class="mw-redirect" title="Solomon Bandaranaike">S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike</a> (former Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Ceylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a>), <a href="/wiki/Norman_Washington_Manley" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Washington Manley">Norman Washington Manley</a> of Jamaica,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eric_Williams" title="Eric Williams">Eric Williams</a> (Prime Minister of Trinidad and Tobago), <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Pablo_Kuczynski" title="Pedro Pablo Kuczynski">Pedro Pablo Kuczynski</a> (former President of Peru), <a href="/wiki/Abhisit_Vejjajiva" title="Abhisit Vejjajiva">Abhisit Vejjajiva</a> (former Prime Minister of Thailand) and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> (the first President of the United States to have attended Oxford; he attended as a <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholar" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodes Scholar">Rhodes Scholar</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Mutambara" title="Arthur Mutambara">Arthur Mutambara</a> (Deputy Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>), was a <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholar" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodes Scholar">Rhodes Scholar</a> in 1991. <a href="/wiki/Seretse_Khama" title="Seretse Khama">Seretse Khama</a>, first president of Botswana, spent a year at Balliol College. <a href="/wiki/Festus_Mogae" title="Festus Mogae">Festus Mogae</a> (former president of <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>) was a student at <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Oxford" title="University College, Oxford">University College</a>. The Burmese democracy activist and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>, was a student of St Hugh's College.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jigme_Khesar_Namgyel_Wangchuck" title="Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck">Jigme Khesar Namgyel Wangchuck</a>, the current reigning <a href="/wiki/Druk_Gyalpo" title="Druk Gyalpo">Druk Gyalpo</a> (Dragon King) of <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>, was a member of <a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_College,_Oxford" title="St Peter&#39;s College, Oxford">St Peter's College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:396px;max-width:396px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Lawyers who attended Oxford University</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:131px;max-width:131px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:1_David_Neuberger,_Baron_Neuberger_of_Abbotsbury_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/1_David_Neuberger%2C_Baron_Neuberger_of_Abbotsbury_2016.jpg/258px-1_David_Neuberger%2C_Baron_Neuberger_of_Abbotsbury_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3540" data-file-height="4912" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Lord_Neuberger" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Neuberger">Lord Neuberger</a>, <a data-file-height="3264" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Dworkin" title="Ronald Dworkin">Ronald Dworkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_College,_Oxford" title="Magdalen College, Oxford">Magdalen College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Elena_Kagan_Official_SCOTUS_Portrait_(2013).jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
