data-file-height="3600" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Elena_Kagan" title="Elena Kagan">Elena Kagan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worcester_College,_Oxford" title="Worcester College, Oxford">Worcester College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div><p>Oxford has produced a large number of distinguished <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judge" title="Judge">judges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyers</a> around the world. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bingham,_Baron_Bingham_of_Cornhill" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Bingham, Baron Bingham of Cornhill">Lords Bingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Denning,_Baron_Denning" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred Denning, Baron Denning">Denning</a>, commonly recognised as two of the most influential English judges in the history of the <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> both studied at Oxford. Within the United Kingdom, five of the current <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Justice of the Supreme Court of the United Kingdom">Justices of the Supreme Court</a> are Oxford-educated: <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Sumption,_Lord_Sumption" title="Jonathan Sumption, Lord Sumption">Jonathan Sumption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Mance,_Baron_Mance" title="Jonathan Mance, Baron Mance">Jonathan Mance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Wilson,_Lord_Wilson_of_Culworth" title="Nicholas Wilson, Lord Wilson of Culworth">Nicholas Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Reed,_Lord_Reed" title="Robert Reed, Lord Reed">Robert Reed</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Briggs,_Lord_Briggs_of_Westbourne" title="Michael Briggs, Lord Briggs of Westbourne">Michael Briggs</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> retired Justices include <a href="/wiki/David_Neuberger,_Baron_Neuberger_of_Abbotsbury" title="David Neuberger, Baron Neuberger of Abbotsbury">David Neuberger</a> (President of the Supreme Court 2012–2017), <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rodger,_Baron_Rodger_of_Earlsferry" title="Alan Rodger, Baron Rodger of Earlsferry">Alan Rodger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Saville,_Baron_Saville_of_Newdigate" title="Mark Saville, Baron Saville of Newdigate">Mark Saville,</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Dyson,_Lord_Dyson" title="John Dyson, Lord Dyson">John Dyson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Brown,_Baron_Brown_of_Eaton-under-Heywood" title="Simon Brown, Baron Brown of Eaton-under-Heywood">Simon Brown</a>. The twelve <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellors</a> and nine <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chief_Justice_of_England_and_Wales" title="Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales">Lord Chief Justices</a> that have been educated at Oxford include <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bingham,_Baron_Bingham_of_Cornhill" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Bingham, Baron Bingham of Cornhill">Thomas Bingham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Buckmaster,_1st_Viscount_Buckmaster" title="Stanley Buckmaster, 1st Viscount Buckmaster">Stanley Buckmaster,</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_More" title="Thomas More">Thomas More</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Thomas Wolsey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Simonds,_1st_Viscount_Simonds" title="Gavin Simonds, 1st Viscount Simonds">Gavin Simonds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The twenty-two <a href="/wiki/Law_Lords" class="mw-redirect" title="Law Lords">Law Lords</a> count amongst them <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Hoffmann,_Baron_Hoffmann" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonard Hoffmann, Baron Hoffmann">Leonard Hoffmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Diplock,_Baron_Diplock" title="Kenneth Diplock, Baron Diplock">Kenneth Diplock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wilberforce,_Baron_Wilberforce" title="Richard Wilberforce, Baron Wilberforce">Richard Wilberforce</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Atkin,_Baron_Atkin" title="James Atkin, Baron Atkin">James Atkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Brown,_Baron_Brown_of_Eaton-under-Heywood" title="Simon Brown, Baron Brown of Eaton-under-Heywood">Simon Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Browne-Wilkinson,_Baron_Browne-Wilkinson" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolas Browne-Wilkinson, Baron Browne-Wilkinson">Nicolas Browne-Wilkinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Goff,_Baron_Goff_of_Chieveley" title="Robert Goff, Baron Goff of Chieveley">Robert Goff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Hutton,_Baron_Hutton" title="Brian Hutton, Baron Hutton">Brian Hutton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Mance,_Baron_Mance" title="Jonathan Mance, Baron Mance">Jonathan Mance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rodger,_Baron_Rodger_of_Earlsferry" title="Alan Rodger, Baron Rodger of Earlsferry">Alan Rodger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Saville,_Baron_Saville_of_Newdigate" title="Mark Saville, Baron Saville of Newdigate">Mark Saville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Scarman,_Baron_Scarman" title="Leslie Scarman, Baron Scarman">Leslie Scarman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johan_Steyn,_Baron_Steyn" title="Johan Steyn, Baron Steyn">Johan Steyn</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Master_of_the_Rolls" title="Master of the Rolls">Master of the Rolls</a> include <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Denning,_Baron_Denning" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred Denning, Baron Denning">Alfred Denning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Greene,_1st_Baron_Greene" title="Wilfred Greene, 1st Baron Greene">Wilfred Greene</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-:2_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lord_Justice_of_Appeal" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Justice of Appeal">Lord Justices of Appeal</a> include <a href="/wiki/John_Laws_(judge)" title="John Laws (judge)">John Laws</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Leveson" title="Brian Leveson">Brian Leveson</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Mummery" title="John Mummery">John Mummery</a>. The British Government's <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_for_England_and_Wales" title="Attorney General for England and Wales">Attorneys General</a> have included <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Grieve" title="Dominic Grieve">Dominic Grieve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Lyell,_Baron_Lyell_of_Markyate" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas Lyell, Baron Lyell of Markyate">Nicholas Lyell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Mayhew" title="Patrick Mayhew">Patrick Mayhew</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Hobson_(politician)" title="John Hobson (politician)">John Hobson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Manningham-Buller,_1st_Viscount_Dilhorne" title="Reginald Manningham-Buller, 1st Viscount Dilhorne">Reginald Manningham-Buller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Heald" title="Lionel Heald">Lionel Heald</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Soskice,_Baron_Stow_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Frank Soskice, Baron Stow Hill">Frank Soskice</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Maxwell_Fyfe,_1st_Earl_of_Kilmuir" title="David Maxwell Fyfe, 1st Earl of Kilmuir">David Maxwell Fyfe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Somervell,_Baron_Somervell_of_Harrow" title="Donald Somervell, Baron Somervell of Harrow">Donald Somervell</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Jowitt,_1st_Earl_Jowitt" title="William Jowitt, 1st Earl Jowitt">William Jowitt</a>; <a href="/wiki/Director_of_Public_Prosecutions_(England_and_Wales)" title="Director of Public Prosecutions (England and Wales)">Directors of Public Prosecutions</a> include Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hetherington" title="Thomas Hetherington">Thomas Hetherington</a> QC, Dame <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Mills" title="Barbara Mills">Barbara Mills</a> QC and Sir <a href="/wiki/Keir_Starmer" title="Keir Starmer">Keir Starmer</a> QC.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, three of the nine incumbent <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Justice of the Supreme Court of the United States">Justices of the Supreme Court</a> are Oxonians, namely <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Breyer" title="Stephen Breyer">Stephen Breyer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elena_Kagan" title="Elena Kagan">Elena Kagan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Neil_Gorsuch" title="Neil Gorsuch">Neil Gorsuch</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> retired Justices include <a href="/wiki/John_Marshall_Harlan_II" class="mw-redirect" title="John Marshall Harlan II">John Marshall Harlan II</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Souter" title="David Souter">David Souter</a><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Byron_White" title="Byron White">Byron White</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Internationally, Oxonians Sir <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Waldock" title="Humphrey Waldock">Humphrey Waldock</a><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> served in the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>; <a href="/wiki/Akua_Kuenyehia" title="Akua Kuenyehia">Akua Kuenyehia</a>, sat in the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>; Sir <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Bratza" title="Nicolas Bratza">Nicolas Bratza</a><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mahoney_(English_judge)" title="Paul Mahoney (English judge)">Paul Mahoney</a> sat in the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a>; <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Hayne" title="Kenneth Hayne">Kenneth Hayne</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dyson_Heydon" title="Dyson Heydon">Dyson Heydon</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Keane" title="Patrick Keane">Patrick Keane</a> sat in the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia" title="High Court of Australia">High Court of Australia</a>; both <a href="/wiki/Kailas_Nath_Wanchoo" title="Kailas Nath Wanchoo">Kailas Nath Wanchoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/A._N._Ray" title="A. N. Ray">A. N. Ray</a> served as Chief Justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India" title="Supreme Court of India">Supreme Court of India</a>; in Hong Kong, <a href="/wiki/Aarif_Barma" title="Aarif Barma">Aarif Barma</a> and Doreen Le Pichon<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> currently serve in the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_(Hong_Kong)" title="Court of Appeal (Hong Kong)">Court of Appeal (Hong Kong)</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ching" title="Charles Ching">Charles Ching</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Litton" title="Henry Litton">Henry Litton</a> both served as Permanent Judges of the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Final_Appeal_of_Hong_Kong" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Final Appeal of Hong Kong">Court of Final Appeal of Hong Kong</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> six <a href="/wiki/Puisne_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="Puisne Justice">puisne justices</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a> and a chief justice of the now defunct <a href="/wiki/Federal_Court_of_Canada" title="Federal Court of Canada">Federal Court of Canada</a> were also educated at Oxford.
</p><p>The list of noted <a href="/wiki/Legal_scholar" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal scholar">legal scholar</a>s includes <a href="/wiki/H._L._A._Hart" title="H. L. A. Hart">H. L. A. Hart</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hodgson_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodgson-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Dworkin" title="Ronald Dworkin">Ronald Dworkin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hodgson_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodgson-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Waldron" title="Jeremy Waldron">Jeremy Waldron</a>, <a href="/wiki/A._V._Dicey" title="A. V. Dicey">A. V. Dicey</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Blackstone" title="William Blackstone">William Blackstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Gardner_(legal_philosopher)" title="John Gardner (legal philosopher)">John Gardner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Endicott" title="Timothy Endicott">Timothy Endicott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Birks" title="Peter Birks">Peter Birks</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Finnis" title="John Finnis">John Finnis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Ashworth" title="Andrew Ashworth">Andrew Ashworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Raz" title="Joseph Raz">Joseph Raz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Green_(philosopher)" title="Leslie Green (philosopher)">Leslie Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Honor%C3%A9" title="Tony Honoré">Tony Honoré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_MacCormick" title="Neil MacCormick">Neil MacCormick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Collins" title="Hugh Collins">Hugh Collins</a>. Other distinguished practitioners who have attended Oxford include <a href="/wiki/David_Pannick,_Baron_Pannick" title="David Pannick, Baron Pannick">Lord Pannick</a> <a href="/wiki/Qc" class="mw-redirect" title="Qc">QC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Robertson" title="Geoffrey Robertson">Geoffrey Robertson</a> QC, <a href="/wiki/Amal_Clooney" title="Amal Clooney">Amal Clooney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Faulks,_Baron_Faulks" title="Edward Faulks, Baron Faulks">Lord Faulks</a> QC, and <a href="/wiki/Dinah_Rose" title="Dinah Rose">Dinah Rose</a> QC.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematics_and_sciences">Mathematics and sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Mathematics and sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:403px;max-width:403px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Scientists who attended Oxford University</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:135px;max-width:135px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hawking.StarChild.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Stephen_Hawking.StarChild.jpg/133px-Stephen_Hawking.StarChild.jpg" width="133" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Stephen_Hawking.StarChild.jpg/200px-Stephen_Hawking.StarChild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/Stephen_Hawking.StarChild.jpg 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="359" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Oxford" title="University College, Oxford">University College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:125px;max-width:125px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg/123px-Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg" width="123" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg/185px-Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg/246px-Tim_Berners-Lee_CP_2_head_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1111" data-file-height="1716" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Queen%27s_College,_Oxford" title="The Queen&#39;s College, Oxford">The Queen's College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:137px;max-width:137px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3f/Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg/135px-Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg" width="135" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3f/Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg/203px-Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3f/Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg/270px-Dorothy_Hodgkin_Nobel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="396" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Hodgkin" title="Dorothy Hodgkin">Dorothy Hodgkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerville_College,_Oxford" title="Somerville College, Oxford">Somerville College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Three Oxford mathematicians, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Atiyah" title="Michael Atiyah">Michael Atiyah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Quillen" title="Daniel Quillen">Daniel Quillen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Donaldson" title="Simon Donaldson">Simon Donaldson</a>, have won <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medals</a>, often called the "Nobel Prize for mathematics". <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Wiles" title="Andrew Wiles">Andrew Wiles</a>, who proved <a href="/wiki/Fermat%27s_Last_Theorem" title="Fermat&#39;s Last Theorem">Fermat's Last Theorem</a>, was educated at Oxford and is currently the <a href="/wiki/Regius_Professor" title="Regius Professor">Regius Professor</a> and Royal Society Research Professor in Mathematics at Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-Wiles_Regius_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiles_Regius-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marcus_du_Sautoy" title="Marcus du Sautoy">Marcus du Sautoy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">Roger Penrose</a> are both currently mathematics professors, and <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Stedall" title="Jackie Stedall">Jackie Stedall</a> was a professor of the university. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Wolfram" title="Stephen Wolfram">Stephen Wolfram</a>, chief designer of <a href="/wiki/Mathematica" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematica">Mathematica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Alpha" title="Wolfram Alpha">Wolfram Alpha</a> studied at the university, along with <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> inventor of the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edgar_F._Codd" title="Edgar F. Codd">Edgar F. Codd</a>, inventor of <a href="/wiki/Relational_model" title="Relational model">the relational model of data</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ACM_Turing_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACM_Turing-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hoare" title="Tony Hoare">Tony Hoare</a>, programming languages pioneer and inventor of <a href="/wiki/Quicksort" title="Quicksort">Quicksort</a>.
</p><p>The university is associated with eleven winners of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a>, five in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">physics</a> and sixteen in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Scientists who performed research in Oxford include chemist <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Hodgkin" title="Dorothy Hodgkin">Dorothy Hodgkin</a> who received her Nobel Prize for "determinations by X-ray techniques of the structures of important biochemical substances".<sup id="cite_ref-nobel_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dawkins" title="Richard Dawkins">Richard Dawkins</a><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Soddy" title="Frederick Soddy">Frederick Soddy</a><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> studied at the university and returned for research purposes. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">Robert Hooke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Edwin Hubble</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a><sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> all studied in Oxford.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Boyle" title="Robert Boyle">Robert Boyle</a>, a founder of modern chemistry, never formally studied or held a post within the university, but resided within the city to be part of the scientific community and was awarded an honorary degree.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Notable scientists who spent brief periods at Oxford include <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> developer of <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general theory of relativity</a> and the concept of <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photons</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Schr%C3%B6dinger" title="Erwin Schrödinger">Erwin Schrödinger</a> who formulated the <a href="/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation" title="Schrödinger equation">Schrödinger equation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger%27s_cat" title="Schrödinger&#39;s cat">Schrödinger's cat</a> thought experiment. Structural engineer <a href="/wiki/Roma_Agrawal" title="Roma Agrawal">Roma Agrawal</a>, responsible for London's iconic <a href="/wiki/The_Shard" title="The Shard">Shard</a>, attributes her love of engineering to a summer placement during her undergraduate physics degree at Oxford. 
</p><p>Economists <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Marshall" title="Alfred Marshall">Alfred Marshall</a>, <a href="/wiki/E._F._Schumacher" title="E. F. Schumacher">E. F. Schumacher</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a> all spent time at Oxford.
</p>
<h3><span id="Literature.2C_music.2C_and_drama"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature,_music,_and_drama">Literature, music, and drama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Literature, music, and drama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:434px;max-width:434px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Literary figures who attended Oxford University</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:113px;max-width:113px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Wilde_portrait_by_Napoleon_Sarony_-_albumen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Oscar_Wilde_portrait_by_Napoleon_Sarony_-_albumen.jpg/167px-Oscar_Wilde_portrait_by_Napoleon_Sarony_-_albumen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Oscar_Wilde_portrait_by_Napoleon_Sarony_-_albumen.jpg/222px-Oscar_Wilde_portrait_by_Napoleon_Sarony_-_albumen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2190" data-file-height="3640" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_College,_Oxford" title="Magdalen College, Oxford">Magdalen College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:129px;max-width:129px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Tolkien_1916.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Tolkien_1916.jpg/127px-Tolkien_1916.jpg" width="127" height="184" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Tolkien_1916.jpg/191px-Tolkien_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Tolkien_1916.jpg/254px-Tolkien_1916.jpg 2x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="473" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/J.R.R._Tolkien" class="mw-redirect" title="J.R.R. Tolkien">J.R.R. Tolkien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_College,_Oxford" title="Exeter College, Oxford">Exeter College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:186px;max-width:186px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vera_Brittain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Vera_Brittain.jpg/184px-Vera_Brittain.jpg" width="184" height="184" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Vera_Brittain.jpg/276px-Vera_Brittain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Vera_Brittain.jpg/368px-Vera_Brittain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="390" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Vera_Brittain" title="Vera Brittain">Vera Brittain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerville_College,_Oxford" title="Somerville College, Oxford">Somerville College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>The long list of writers associated with Oxford includes <a href="/wiki/John_Fowles" title="John Fowles">John Fowles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Seuss" title="Dr. Seuss">Theodor Geisel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Middleton" title="Thomas Middleton">Thomas Middleton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr_Samuel_Johnson" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr Samuel Johnson">Samuel Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Hitchens" title="Christopher Hitchens">Christopher Hitchens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Graves" title="Robert Graves">Robert Graves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh">Evelyn Waugh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Carroll" title="Lewis Carroll">Lewis Carroll</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aldous_Huxley" title="Aldous Huxley">Aldous Huxley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/C._S._Lewis" title="C. S. Lewis">C. S. Lewis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Graham_Greene" title="Graham Greene">Graham Greene</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/V.S.Naipaul" class="mw-redirect" title="V.S.Naipaul">V.S.Naipaul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vera_Brittain" title="Vera Brittain">Vera Brittain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_L._Sayers" title="Dorothy L. Sayers">Dorothy L. Sayers</a>, <a href="/wiki/A.S._Byatt" class="mw-redirect" title="A.S. Byatt">A.S. Byatt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iris_Murdoch" title="Iris Murdoch">Iris Murdoch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Pullman" title="Philip Pullman">Philip Pullman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Heller" title="Joseph Heller">Joseph Heller</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vikram_Seth" title="Vikram Seth">Vikram Seth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> the poets <a href="/wiki/Percy_Bysshe_Shelley" title="Percy Bysshe Shelley">Percy Bysshe Shelley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Donne" title="John Donne">John Donne</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._E._Housman" title="A. E. Housman">A. E. Housman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Manley_Hopkins" title="Gerard Manley Hopkins">Gerard Manley Hopkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/W._H._Auden" title="W. H. Auden">W. H. Auden</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/T._S._Eliot" title="T. S. Eliot">T. S. Eliot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Perriam" title="Wendy Perriam">Wendy Perriam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philip_Larkin" title="Philip Larkin">Philip Larkin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> and seven <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Poet Laureate">poets laureate</a>: <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Warton" title="Thomas Warton">Thomas Warton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henry_James_Pye" title="Henry James Pye">Henry James Pye</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Southey" title="Robert Southey">Robert Southey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bridges" title="Robert Bridges">Robert Bridges</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Day-Lewis" title="Cecil Day-Lewis">Cecil Day-Lewis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Betjeman" title="John Betjeman">Sir John Betjeman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Motion" title="Andrew Motion">Andrew Motion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Composers <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Parry" title="Hubert Parry">Hubert Parry</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Butterworth" title="George Butterworth">George Butterworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Taverner" title="John Taverner">John Taverner</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Walton" title="William Walton">William Walton</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Whitbourn" title="James Whitbourn">James Whitbourn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">Andrew Lloyd Webber</a> have all been involved with the university.
</p><p>Actors <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Grant" title="Hugh Grant">Hugh Grant</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-New_College_alumni_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_College_alumni-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kate_Beckinsale" title="Kate Beckinsale">Kate Beckinsale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-New_College_alumni_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_College_alumni-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rosamund_Pike" title="Rosamund Pike">Rosamund Pike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felicity_Jones" title="Felicity Jones">Felicity Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gemma_Chan" title="Gemma Chan">Gemma Chan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dudley_Moore" title="Dudley Moore">Dudley Moore</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Palin" title="Michael Palin">Michael Palin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Jones" title="Terry Jones">Terry Jones</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anna_Popplewell" title="Anna Popplewell">Anna Popplewell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rowan_Atkinson" title="Rowan Atkinson">Rowan Atkinson</a> were undergraduates at the university, as were filmmakers <a href="/wiki/Ken_Loach" title="Ken Loach">Ken Loach</a><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Curtis" title="Richard Curtis">Richard Curtis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;max-width:372px"><div College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:145px;max-width:145px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Rosamund_Pike_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Oxford has also produced at least 12 <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saints</a>, 19 <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_cardinals" title="List of English cardinals">English cardinals</a>, and 20 <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishops of Canterbury</a>, the most recent Archbishop being <a href="/wiki/Rowan_Williams" title="Rowan Williams">Rowan Williams</a>, who studied at <a href="/wiki/Wadham_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Wadham College">Wadham College</a> and was later a Canon Professor at <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford" title="Christ Church, Oxford">Christ Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Duns_Scotus" title="Duns Scotus">Duns Scotus</a>' teaching is commemorated with a monument in the University Church of St. Mary. Religious reformer <a href="/wiki/John_Wycliffe" title="John Wycliffe">John Wycliffe</a> was an Oxford scholar, for a time Master of <a href="/wiki/Balliol_College,_Oxford" title="Balliol College, Oxford">Balliol College</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Colet" title="John Colet">John Colet</a>, Christian humanist, <a href="/wiki/Dean_of_St_Paul%27s" title="Dean of St Paul&#39;s">Dean of St Paul's</a>, and friend of <a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus</a>, studied at <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_College,_Oxford" title="Magdalen College, Oxford">Magdalen College</a>. Several of the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Divines" title="Caroline Divines">Caroline Divines</a> e.g. in particular <a href="/wiki/William_Laud" title="William Laud">William Laud</a> as President of St. John's and Chancellor of the University, and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Jurors" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Jurors">Non-Jurors</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ken" title="Thomas Ken">Thomas Ken</a> had close Oxford connections.The founder of <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a>, studied at Christ Church and was elected a fellow of <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_College,_Oxford" title="Lincoln College, Oxford">Lincoln College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> The Oxford Movement (1833–1846) was closely associated with the Oriel Fellows <a href="/wiki/John_Henry_Newman" title="John Henry Newman">John Henry Newman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Bouverie_Pusey" title="Edward Bouverie Pusey">Edward Bouverie Pusey</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Keble" title="John Keble">John Keble</a>. Other religious figures were <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Nasir_Ahmad" title="Mirza Nasir Ahmad">Mirza Nasir Ahmad</a>, the third <a href="/wiki/Khalifatul_Masih" class="mw-redirect" title="Khalifatul Masih">Caliph</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Muslim_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmadiyya Muslim Community">Ahmadiyya Muslim Community</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shoghi_Effendi" title="Shoghi Effendi">Shoghi Effendi</a>, one of the appointed leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Baha%27i_faith" class="mw-redirect" title="Baha&#39;i faith">Baha'i faith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Cordeiro" title="Joseph Cordeiro">Joseph Cordeiro</a>, the only Pakistani Catholic cardinal.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophy">Philosophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Philosophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:419px;max-width:419px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Philosophers who attended Oxford University</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:121px;max-width:121px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller,_National_Portrait_Gallery,_London.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller%2C_National_Portrait_Gallery%2C_London.JPG/119px-John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller%2C_National_Portrait_Gallery%2C_London.JPG" width="119" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller%2C_National_Portrait_Gallery%2C_London.JPG/179px-John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller%2C_National_Portrait_Gallery%2C_London.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller%2C_National_Portrait_Gallery%2C_London.JPG/238px-John_Locke%27s_Kit-cat_portrait_by_Godfrey_Kneller%2C_National_Portrait_Gallery%2C_London.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2056" data-file-height="3088" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/John_Locke" title="John Locke">John Locke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford" title="Christ Church, Oxford">Christ Church</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:140px;max-width:140px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg/138px-OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg" width="138" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg/207px-OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg/276px-OnoraONeillChairingWCITColloquiumHouseOfLords26June2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1613" data-file-height="2098" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Onora_O%27Neill" title="Onora O&#39;Neill">Onora O'Neill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerville_College,_Oxford" title="Somerville College, Oxford">Somerville College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Hobbes.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Thomas_Hobbes.jpeg/150px-Thomas_Hobbes.jpeg" width="150" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Thomas_Hobbes.jpeg/225px-Thomas_Hobbes.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Thomas_Hobbes.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="275" data-file-height="326" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hobbes" title="Thomas Hobbes">Thomas Hobbes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertford_College,_Oxford" title="Hertford College, Oxford">Hertford College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Oxford's philosophical tradition started in the medieval era, with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Grosseteste" title="Robert Grosseteste">Robert Grosseteste</a><sup id="cite_ref-phil-history_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phil-history-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/William_of_Ockham" title="William of Ockham">William of Ockham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-phil-history_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phil-history-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> commonly known for <a href="/wiki/Occam%27s_razor" title="Occam&#39;s razor">Occam's razor</a>, among those teaching at the university. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hobbes" title="Thomas Hobbes">Thomas Hobbes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Bentham" title="Jeremy Bentham">Jeremy Bentham</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Empiricism" title="Empiricism">empiricist</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Locke" title="John Locke">John Locke</a> received degrees from Oxford. Though the latter's main works were written after leaving Oxford, Locke was heavily influenced by his twelve years at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-phil-history_233-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phil-history-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oxford philosophers of the 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Ryle" title="Gilbert Ryle">Gilbert Ryle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-phil-history_233-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phil-history-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Concept_of_Mind" title="The Concept of Mind">The Concept of Mind</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Derek_Parfit" title="Derek Parfit">Derek Parfit</a>, who specialised in personal identity. Other commonly read modern philosophers to have studied at the university include <a href="/wiki/A._J._Ayer" title="A. J. Ayer">A. J. Ayer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-phil-history_233-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phil-history-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Anscombe" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth Anscombe">Elizabeth Anscombe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Grice" title="Paul Grice">Paul Grice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iris_Murdoch" title="Iris Murdoch">Iris Murdoch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Nagel" title="Thomas Nagel">Thomas Nagel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Williams" title="Bernard Williams">Bernard Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Nozick" title="Robert Nozick">Robert Nozick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onora_O%27Neill" title="Onora O&#39;Neill">Onora O'Neill</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Rawls" title="John Rawls">John Rawls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Sandel" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Sandel">Michael Sandel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Singer" title="Peter Singer">Peter Singer</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Searle" title="John Searle">John Searle</a>, presenter of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_room" title="Chinese room">Chinese room</a> thought experiment, studied and began his academic career at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Likewise, <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Foot" title="Philippa Foot">Philippa Foot</a>, the creator of the famous <a href="/wiki/Trolley_problem" title="Trolley problem">trolley problem</a>, studied and taught at Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-Philippa_Foot_1978_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philippa_Foot_1978-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Matthew_Pinsent_%28flipped_right-facing%29.jpg/168px-Matthew_Pinsent_%28flipped_right-facing%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Matthew_Pinsent_%28flipped_right-facing%29.jpg/224px-Matthew_Pinsent_%28flipped_right-facing%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="916" data-file-height="1376" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Matthew_Pinsent" title="Matthew Pinsent">Matthew Pinsent</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Catherine%27s_College,_Oxford" title="St Catherine&#39;s College, Oxford">St Catherine's College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Some 150 Olympic medal-winners have academic connections with the university, including <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Pinsent" title="Matthew Pinsent">Sir Matthew Pinsent</a>, quadruple gold-medallist rower.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Other sporting connections include <a href="/wiki/Imran_Khan" title="Imran Khan">Imran Khan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Famous_22-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Famous-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rowers from Oxford who have won gold at the Olympics or World Championships include <a href="/wiki/Michael_Blomquist" title="Michael Blomquist">Michael Blomquist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Coode" title="Ed Coode">Ed Coode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Davidge" title="Chris Davidge">Chris Davidge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Edwards_(rower)" title="Hugh Edwards (rower)">Hugh Edwards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Flickinger" title="Jason Flickinger">Jason Flickinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Foster" title="Tim Foster">Tim Foster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Liwski" title="Christopher Liwski">Christopher Liwski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Pinsent" title="Matthew Pinsent">Matthew Pinsent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Reed" title="Pete Reed">Pete Reed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Searle" title="Jonny Searle">Jonny Searle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Triggs_Hodge" title="Andrew Triggs Hodge">Andrew Triggs Hodge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jake_Wetzel" title="Jake Wetzel">Jake Wetzel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wherley" title="Michael Wherley">Michael Wherley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barney_Williams" title="Barney Williams">Barney Williams</a>. Many Oxford graduates have also risen to the highest echelon in cricket: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Altham" title="Harry Altham">Harry Altham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Bosanquet_(cricketer)" title="Bernard Bosanquet (cricketer)">Bernard Bosanquet</a> (inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Googly" title="Googly">googly</a>), <a href="/wiki/Colin_Cowdrey" title="Colin Cowdrey">Colin Cowdrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Crutchley" title="Gerry Crutchley">Gerry Crutchley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dalrymple" title="Jamie Dalrymple">Jamie Dalrymple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Donnelly_(cricketer)" title="Martin Donnelly (cricketer)">Martin Donnelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/R._E._Foster" title="R. E. Foster">R. E. Foster</a> (the only man to captain England at both cricket and football), <a href="/wiki/C._B._Fry" title="C. B. Fry">C. B. Fry</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Harris,_4th_Baron_Harris" title="George Harris, 4th Baron Harris">George Harris</a> (also served in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>), <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Jardine" title="Douglas Jardine">Douglas Jardine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Jardine" title="Malcolm Jardine">Malcolm Jardine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imran_Khan" title="Imran Khan">Imran Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Melville" title="Alan Melville">Alan Melville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iftikhar_Ali_Khan_Pataudi" title="Iftikhar Ali Khan Pataudi">Iftikhar Ali Khan Pataudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansoor_Ali_Khan_Pataudi" title="Mansoor Ali Khan Pataudi">Mansoor Ali Khan Pataudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/M._J._K._Smith" title="M. J. K. Smith">M. J. K. Smith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pelham_Warner" title="Pelham Warner">Pelham Warner</a>.
</p><p>Oxford students have also excelled in other sports. Such alumni include <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> player <a href="/wiki/Myron_Rolle" title="Myron Rolle">Myron Rolle</a> (<a href="/wiki/NFL" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL">NFL</a> player); Olympic gold medalists in athletics <a href="/wiki/David_Hemery" title="David Hemery">David Hemery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lovelock" title="Jack Lovelock">Jack Lovelock</a>; basketball players <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bradley" title="Bill Bradley">Bill Bradley</a> (<a href="/wiki/US_Senator" class="mw-redirect" title="US Senator">US Senator</a> and <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> player) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Thomas_McMillen" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Thomas McMillen">Charles Thomas McMillen</a> (<a href="/wiki/US_Congressman" class="mw-redirect" title="US Congressman">US Congressman</a> and <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> player); <a href="/wiki/Figure_skater" class="mw-redirect" title="Figure skater">figure skater</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Misha_Petkevich" title="John Misha Petkevich">John Misha Petkevich</a> (national champion); footballers <a href="/wiki/John_Bain_(footballer,_born_1854)" title="John Bain (footballer, born 1854)">John Bain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Wreford-Brown" title="Charles Wreford-Brown">Charles Wreford-Brown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cuthbert_Ottaway" title="Cuthbert Ottaway">Cuthbert Ottaway</a>; fencer <a href="/wiki/Allan_Jay" title="Allan Jay">Allan Jay</a> (world champion and five-time Olympian); <a href="/wiki/Modern_pentathlete" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern pentathlete">modern pentathlete</a> <a href="/wiki/Steph_Cook" title="Steph Cook">Steph Cook</a> (Olympic gold medalist); <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby footballers</a> <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Barnes" title="Stuart Barnes">Stuart Barnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Danielli" title="Simon Danielli">Simon Danielli</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Humphreys_(rugby_union)" title="David Humphreys (rugby union)">David Humphreys</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Kirk" title="David Kirk">David Edward Kirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Oliver" title="Anton Oliver">Anton Oliver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Poulton-Palmer" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronald Poulton-Palmer">Ronald Poulton-Palmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Roff" title="Joe Roff">Joe Roff</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_Webb_Ellis" title="William Webb Ellis">William Webb Ellis</a> (allegedly the inventor of <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby football</a>); runner <a href="/wiki/Roger_Bannister" title="Roger Bannister">Sir Roger Gilbert Bannister</a> (who ran the first sub-four-minute mile), <a href="/wiki/FIS_Freestyle_Skiing_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FIS Freestyle Skiing World Cup">World Cup freestyle skier</a> <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Max_Riley" title="Ryan Max Riley">Ryan Max Riley</a> (national champion); and tennis player <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Bruce,_3rd_Baron_Aberdare" title="Clarence Bruce, 3rd Baron Aberdare">Clarence Bruce</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adventure_and_exploration">Adventure and exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Adventure and exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:405px;max-width:405px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Explorers and adventurers who attended Oxford University</div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:133px;max-width:133px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg/131px-BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg" width="131" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg/197px-BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg/262px-BellK_218_Gertrude_Bell_in_Iraq_in_1909_age_41.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2647" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Bell" title="Gertrude Bell">Gertrude Bell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Margaret_Hall,_Oxford" title="Lady Margaret Hall, Oxford"> Lady Margaret Hall</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg/130px-With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg" width="130" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg/195px-With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg/260px-With_Lawrence_in_Arabia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="366" data-file-height="488" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/T._E._Lawrence" title="T. E. Lawrence">T. E. Lawrence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesus_College,_Oxford" title="Jesus College, Oxford">Jesus College</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:134px;max-width:134px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg/132px-William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg" width="132" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg/198px-William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg/264px-William_Segar_Sir_Walter_Raleigh_1598.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2286" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh"> Sir Walter Raleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriel_College,_Oxford" title="Oriel College, Oxford">Oriel College</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Three of the most well-known <a href="/wiki/Adventurers" class="mw-redirect" title="Adventurers">adventurers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Explorers" class="mw-redirect" title="Explorers">explorers</a> who attended Oxford are <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a>, one of the most notable figures of the <a href="/wiki/Elizabethan_era" title="Elizabethan era">Elizabethan era</a>, <a href="/wiki/T._E._Lawrence" title="T. E. Lawrence">T. E. Lawrence</a>, whose life was the basis of the 1962 film <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawrence of Arabia">Lawrence of Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Coryat" title="Thomas Coryat">Thomas Coryat</a>. The latter, the author of "<a href="/wiki/Coryat%27s_Crudities" title="Coryat&#39;s Crudities">Coryat's Crudities hastily gobbled up in Five Months Travels in France, Italy, &amp;c'</a>" (1611) and <a href="/wiki/Court_jester" class="mw-redirect" title="Court jester">court jester</a> of <a href="/wiki/Henry_Frederick,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Henry Frederick, Prince of Wales">Henry Frederick, Prince of Wales</a>, is credited with introducing the table <a href="/wiki/Fork" title="Fork">fork</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umbrella" title="Umbrella">umbrella</a> to England and being the first Briton to do a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a> of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other notable figures include <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Bell" title="Gertrude Bell">Gertrude Bell</a>, an explorer, <a href="/wiki/Archaeologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeologist">archaeologist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">mapper</a> and spy, who, along with <a href="/wiki/T._E._Lawrence" title="T. E. Lawrence">T. E. Lawrence</a>, helped establish the <a href="/wiki/Hashemite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hashemite">Hashemite</a> dynasties in what is today <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and played a major role in establishing and administering the modern state of <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>; <a href="/wiki/Richard_Francis_Burton" title="Richard Francis Burton">Richard Francis Burton</a>, who travelled in disguise to <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a> and journeyed with <a href="/wiki/John_Hanning_Speke" title="John Hanning Speke">John Hanning Speke</a> as the first European explorers to visit the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Lakes of Africa">Great Lakes of Africa</a> in search of the source of the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mountaineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountaineer">mountaineer</a> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bourdillon" title="Tom Bourdillon">Tom Bourdillon</a>, member of the expedition to make the first ascent of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Fleming_(writer)" title="Peter Fleming (writer)">Peter Fleming</a>, adventurer and travel writer and elder brother of <a href="/wiki/Ian_Fleming" title="Ian Fleming">Ian Fleming</a>, creator of <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oxford_in_literature_and_other_media">Oxford in literature and other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Oxford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Oxford in literature and other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg/500px-1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg" width="500" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg/750px-1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg/1000px-1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11316" data-file-height="3918" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1_oxford_aerial_panorama_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>Aerial panorama of the university</center></div></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford_in_popular_culture" title="University of Oxford in popular culture">University of Oxford in popular culture</a></div>
<p>The University of Oxford is the setting for numerous works of fiction. Oxford was mentioned in fiction as early as 1400 when <a href="/wiki/Chaucer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chaucer">Chaucer</a> in his <i><a href="/wiki/Canterbury_Tales" class="mw-redirect" title="Canterbury Tales">Canterbury Tales</a></i> referred to a "Clerk [student] of Oxenford". By 1989, 533 novels based in Oxford had been identified and the number continues to rise.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Famous literary works range from <i><a href="/wiki/Brideshead_Revisited" title="Brideshead Revisited">Brideshead Revisited</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh">Evelyn Waugh</a>, to the trilogy <i><a href="/wiki/His_Dark_Materials" title="His Dark Materials">His Dark Materials</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Pullman" title="Philip Pullman">Philip Pullman</a>, which features an alternate-reality version of the university.
</p><p>Other notable examples include:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Gaudy_Night" title="Gaudy Night">Gaudy Night</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Lord_Peter_Wimsey" title="Lord Peter Wimsey">Lord Peter Wimsey</a> mystery by <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_L._Sayers" title="Dorothy L. Sayers">Dorothy L. Sayers</a> (who was herself a graduate of <a href="/wiki/Somerville_College,_Oxford" title="Somerville College, Oxford">Somerville College</a>).</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Inspector_Morse" title="Inspector Morse">Inspector Morse</a></i> series by <a href="/wiki/Colin_Dexter" title="Colin Dexter">Colin Dexter</a>, and its spin off <a href="/wiki/Lewis_(TV_series)" title="Lewis (TV series)">Lewis</a>, are set in Oxford and frequently refer to the university (although most of the college names are fictional).</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Zuleika_Dobson" title="Zuleika Dobson">Zuleika Dobson</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Max_Beerbohm" title="Max Beerbohm">Max Beerbohm</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Brideshead_Revisited" title="Brideshead Revisited">Brideshead Revisited</a></i> (1981), based on <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh">Waugh's</a> novel; a <a href="/wiki/Miniseries" title="Miniseries">miniseries</a> enormously popular in Britain and America, the film has sometimes been seen as drawing unwanted attention to Oxford's stereotypical reputation as a playground for the <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">upper class</a>. It stars <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Irons" title="Jeremy Irons">Jeremy Irons</a> and most college shots are of <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford" title="Christ Church, Oxford">Christ Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hertford_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Hertford College">Hertford</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(1996_film)" title="True Blue (1996 film)">True Blue</a></i> (1996), about the mutiny at the time of the Oxford-Cambridge <a href="/wiki/Boat_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Boat Race">Boat Race</a> of 1987.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_History_Boys_(film)" title="The History Boys (film)">The History Boys (film)</a></i> (2008), about a group of boys applying to do history at Oxford. Set in 1983 and based on the play by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bennett" title="Alan Bennett">Alan Bennett</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Golden_Compass_(film)" title="The Golden Compass (film)">The Golden Compass (film)</a></i> (2007)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Riot_Club" title="The Riot Club">The Riot Club</a></i> (2014)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Testament_of_Youth_(film)" title="Testament of Youth (film)">Testament of Youth (film)</a></i> (2014), drama film based on the <a href="/wiki/Memoir" title="Memoir">memoir</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Testament_of_Youth" title="Testament of Youth">same name</a> written by <a href="/wiki/Somerville_College,_Oxford" title="Somerville College, Oxford">Somerville</a> alumna <a href="/wiki/Vera_Brittain" title="Vera Brittain">Vera Brittain</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Notable non-fiction works on Oxford include <i>Oxford</i> by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Morris" title="Jan Morris">Jan Morris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-OXCHEPS39-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-OXCHEPS39_82-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Dennis, Farrington; Palfreyman, David (21 February 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://oxcheps.new.ox.ac.uk/MainSite%20pages/Resources/OxCHEPS_OP39.pdf">"OFFA and £6000–9000 tuition fees"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>OxCHEPS Occasional Paper No. 39</i>. Oxford Centre for Higher Education Policy Studies<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 March</span> 2011</span>. <q>Note, however, that any university which does not want funding from HEFCE can, as a private corporation, charge whatever tuition fees it likes (exactly as does, say, the University of Buckingham or BPP University College). Under existing legislation and outside of the influence of the HEFCE-funding mechanism upon universities, Government can no more control university tuition fees than it can dictate the price of socks in Marks &amp; Spencer. Universities are not part of the State and they are not part of the public sector; Government has no reserve powers of intervention even in a failing institution.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=OxCHEPS+Occasional+Paper+No.+39&amp;rft.atitle=OFFA+and+%C2%A36000%E2%80%939000+tuition+fees&amp;rft.date=2011-02-21&amp;rft.aulast=Dennis&amp;rft.aufirst=Farrington&amp;rft.au=Palfreyman%2C+David&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Foxcheps.new.ox.ac.uk%2FMainSite%2520pages%2FResources%2FOxCHEPS_OP39.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Oxford" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
